## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations)
**Analysis**: The task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, a classic problem in dynamics where dv/dt (acceleration) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and external forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic restoring force): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (nonlinear oscillator with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (self-sustained limit cycle, often written as dv_dt = -c0*x + c1*(1 - c2*x**2)*v)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (damping nonlinear in velocity)
- Forced linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven harmonic oscillator)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type instability)
- Pendulum equation: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (nonlinear gravitational restoring force)
- Quadratic drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (anharmonic oscillator with velocity-squared damping)
- Cubic-quintic restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Toda potential: dv_dt = c0 * (exp(-c1 * x) - 1) - c2 * v (exponential lattice oscillator)
- Bistable system (double-well): dv_dt = c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (negative linear stiffness with positive cubic)
- Nonlinear damping with position coupling: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * x**2 (dissipation depending on displacement amplitude)
- Self-excited with sign nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (dry friction limit cycle)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd power series in x (x, x^3, x^5) with negative leading coefficient indicates symmetric nonlinear restoring force (hardening/softening springs)
- Velocity proportional damping: -c * v represents linear energy dissipation
- Limit cycle oscillation: v multiplied by a function of x, e.g., (c1 - c2*x^2)*v, causes small-amplitude growth and large-amplitude decay
- External periodic driving: additive sin/cos terms in t with unknown frequency parameter indicate forced oscillation
- Parametric excitation: x multiplied by time-periodic coefficient like (1 + c1*cos(c2*t))
- Exponential nonlinearity exp(-c*x) or sinh(c*x) appears in molecular and lattice potentials (Toda, double-well models)
- Velocity-dependent nonlinear damping: terms like -c * v^3 or -c * v*|v| model non-viscous drag (air resistance, turbulence)
- Sign functions or absolute values of x or v introduce piecewise behavior for dry friction or asymmetric potentials
- Mixed terms like v * x^2 represent nonlinear dissipation that increases with displacement, common in large-amplitude systems
- Bistable or chaotic systems: positive linear stiffness term +c0*x (unstable equilibrium) combined with negative cubic -c1*x^3 (restoring at large amplitudes)
